--- Commit Message ---
LU-11848 lov: FIEMAP support for PFL and FLR file

* use the high 16 bits of fe_device to record the absolute stripe
  number from the beginning we are processing, so that continuous call
  can resume from the stripe specified by it.

Signed-off-by: Bobi Jam <bobijam@whamcloud.com>

Patch Set 5: Code-Review-1

(3 comments)

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-12-05 16:23:09.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

Unfortunately, after more testing I realize that the mirror number is not enough information to restart the object traversal. In fact, it looks like even without FLR mirrors the handling of PFL files is still not working properly.

I tested this on a 3-component PFL file ("-E1M -c 1 -E16M -c3 -E1G -c4" that was written up to 1G so all components initialized), and while it is showing _some_ of the stripes, it definitely is not showing all of them.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-12-05 16:26:48.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

Also, in case of overstriping with a plain file, it may be that there are multiple stripes within the same component on a single OST index, so that needs to be handled also.

It may be that instead of returning the component index we need to return the stripe number across all components to make sure that the restart happens in the correct place.

For now, however, all of the PFL components are being returned in a single call, so it isn't an issue of restarting, AFAICS.

--- Message (Zhenyu Xu, 2020-12-05 16:42:26.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

> Also, in case of overstriping with a plain file, it may be that
 > there are multiple stripes within the same component on a single
 > OST index, so that needs to be handled also.
 > 
 > It may be that instead of returning the component index we need to
 > return the stripe number across all components to make sure that
 > the restart happens in the correct place.
 > 
 > For now, however, all of the PFL components are being returned in a
 > single call, so it isn't an issue of restarting, AFAICS.

in fiemap_calc_fm_end_offset(), it uses fe_device + fe_logical to determine on which stripe and from where on the device of the stripe to resume the fiemap.

--- Message (Zhenyu Xu, 2020-12-05 16:43:47.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

> Unfortunately, after more testing I realize that the mirror number
 > is not enough information to restart the object traversal. In fact,
 > it looks like even without FLR mirrors the handling of PFL files is
 > still not working properly.
 > 
 > I tested this on a 3-component PFL file ("-E1M -c 1 -E16M -c3 -E1G
 > -c4" that was written up to 1G so all components initialized), and
 > while it is showing _some_ of the stripes, it definitely is not
 > showing all of them.

So I need to find a way to determine from which component I'd resume the fiemap call.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-12-05 19:04:01.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

One option is to just count the OST objects from the start of the layout? That avoids the dependence on the OST device number to restart.

--- Message (Zhenyu Xu, 2020-12-07 02:48:15.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

"count the OST objects" also need 16bits counter as fe_device uses. To record which component to resume the fiemap, I'd have to use another 32bits fe_reserved to record the component id for resuming the fiemap call.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-12-07 09:05:24.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

> "count the OST objects" also need 16bits counter as fe_device uses.
 > To record which component to resume the fiemap, I'd have to use
 > another 32bits fe_reserved to record the component id for resuming
 > the fiemap call.

What I mean a 16-bit count OST of objects from the start of the whole layout, not just the stripe number within the component layout, and don't return the component number at all?  This should be unique across all stripes, and the combination of object number plus device number could be used to detect if the layout changes between calls.

> from 80th extents, for some unknown reason, it goes with OST

I would think that if this is the reason why extents are not being shown, then the extent length should be 2048.  I looked at another test on patch v11, and it failed with:

 > sanity test_130g: @@@@@@ FAIL: filefrag printed only 583 <= 700 extents

but all of the extents are length 1024, so there was no merging.  It seems like a bug in the FIEMAP code that not all of the stripes are shown, unless the actual file does not have $nr stripes in it, but some smaller number?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-12-10 10:07:47.000000000) ---
Patch Set 14:

(2 comments)

I think I've figured out where the problem is.  Lustre should be storing the stripe number with every extent, so that the old (and new) filefrag can just copy fe_device from the last returned extent into the 0th extent on a restart.

This will also fix sanity test_130e, even with old filefrag, since every extent on the same stripe will report the same fe_device.  With old kernels it would print "000x" since the stripe index is not set.  With new kernels + old filefrag it will print "1000x", then "2000y" and "3000z", ..., but it would be the same for every extent.  The new filefrag would not print the high bits, but would otherwise work the same.

Since even the old filefrag will copy fm_extent[i-1].fe_device to fm_extent[0].fe_device (which will contain both the stripe number and OST index), then the kernel should have no problem to restart even for PFL/FLR files with the old filefrag.  It just needs to skip objects until it gets to the same stripe number, and restart there.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-12-10 10:12:31.000000000) ---
Patch Set 14:

> old filefrag will print the whole bits of fe_device, so that this
 > test thinks that extents of OST10001 is different from that of
 > OST0001, and the total extent does not add up, causing test failure.
 > 
 > So with this patch in place which we uses high 16bits of fe_device,
 > we needs at least filefrag 1.45.6.wc3 as well.

It isn't *just* that it is printing "10006" for the first extent, but the kernel is also restarting the FIEMAP incorrectly for the old filefrag:

File size of /mnt/lustre/f130e.sanity is 67043328 (65472 blocks of 1024 bytes)
 ext:     device_logical:        physical_offset: length:  dev: flags:
   0:        0..      63:     554272..    554335:     64: 10006: net
   1:      128..     191:     554336..    554399:     64: 0006: net

The stripe number should be included in each extent.

   :
  34:     4352..    4415:    1186112..   1186175:     64: 0006: net
  35:     4480..    4543:    1186240..   1186303:     64: 0006: net
   :
 254:    32512..   32575:    1220352..   1220415:     64: 0006: net
 255:    32640..   32703:    1220480..   1220543:     64: 0006: net
 256:        0..      63:     554072..    554135:     64: 0007: net
 257:      128..     191:     554136..    554199:     64: 0007: net
   :
 290:     4352..    4415:     923968..    924031:     64: 0007: net
 291:     4480..    4543:     924096..    924159:     64: 0007: net
 292:     4608..    4671:    1186368..   1186431:     64: 10006: net
 293:     4736..    4799:    1186496..   1186559:     64: 0006: net
   :
2302:    32512..   32575:     958208..    958271:     64: 0007: net
2303:    32640..   32703:     958336..    958399:     64: 0007: last,net
/mnt/lustre/f130e.sanity: 43 extents found

As you can see, the kernel correctly returns all of the extents for the object on OST0006, and then starts on the extents for OST0007, but extent #291 is the last one returned by the kernel in that buffer.  When FIEMAP restarts, it incorrectly starts with stripe_idx 0 (OST0006) again at the same offset.  This repeats until it prints 2300+ extents, instead of the expected 512 extents.
